## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of current population P and time t. Classical population ecology provides numerous ODE models relating growth rate to population size, ranging from simple exponential/logistic to more complex forms with Allee effects, predation, and time-dependent carrying capacities.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth common in tumor/microbial populations)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with flexible inflection point)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth with minimum viable population threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (cooperative growth at low densities)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with density-dependent removal)
- Logistic with constant harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (growth with constant removal rate)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * c3 (generalized growth model)
- Time-dependent carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (seasonally or temporally varying environment)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (growth with saturation and mortality)
- Predation sink (Holling Type II): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P / (1 + c3 * P) (logistic growth with saturating predation)
- Power-law growth with ceiling: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P**c3 (generalized birth-death process)
- Oscillatory environment: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (periodic environmental forcing)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Quadratic dependence on P (terms like P - c*P^2) → logistic-type density dependence with intraspecific competition
- Cubic dependence on P (terms like P^2 - c*P^3) → Allee effect where growth requires minimum population density
- Logarithmic coupling log(P) multiplied by P → Gompertz-type growth with multiplicative slowdown near carrying capacity
- Rational form P/(1+c*P) → saturating functional response (Holling Type II) in predator-prey or resource limitation
- Explicit time dependence through trigonometric functions of t → seasonally forced or periodically varying environment
- Growth rate that changes sign at specific P values → existence of equilibrium points (stable/unstable fixed points)
- Fractional power P^c with 0<c<1 → cooperative or sublinear per-capita growth at low densities
- Additive constant term independent of P → external immigration or constant harvesting pressure
- Product of multiple linear factors in P → multiple equilibria with distinct stability properties
- Exponential decay in t multiplied by growth terms → transient dynamics or deteriorating environmental conditions

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P/(c9 + exp(-c10*(-c11 + P)))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and determine if any candidate can match it.

## GT Analysis

Let me simplify the GT:
```
0.1387*(-1 + P/8.038)*(1 - P/70.018)*P + 0.1387*(1 - P/70.018)*P + 0.1387*P/(1 + exp(-8.038*(-0.5894 + P)))
```

Let me expand the first two terms:
- Term 1: `0.1387*(-1 + P/8.038)*(1 - P/70.018)*P`
- Term 2: `0.1387*(1 - P/70.018)*P`
- Term 3: `0.1387*P/(1 + exp(-8.038*(-0.5894 + P)))`

Combining Terms 1 and 2:
`0.1387*(1 - P/70.018)*P * [(-1 + P/8.038) + 1]`
= `0.1387*(1 - P/70.018)*P * (P/8.038)`
= `0.1387*P²/8.038 * (1 - P/70.018)`
= `0.01726*P²*(1 - P/70.018)`
= `0.01726*P² - 0.0002465*P³`

So the GT simplifies to:
**GT = -0.0002465*P³ + 0.01726*P² + 0.1387*P/(1 + exp(-8.038*(P - 0.5894)))**

This is a polynomial in P (cubic) plus a sigmoid-like term. The GT has **no dependence on t**.

Now I need to find candidates that:
1. Can eliminate t-dependence (if present)
2. Can represent: `a*P³ + b*P² + c*P/(1 + exp(d*(P - e)))` or equivalent

The sigmoid term `P/(1+exp(-k*(P-m)))` is tricky. Note that `1/(1+exp(-x))` is a logistic function, not easily represented by exp, sin, log alone.

However, I can rewrite `P/(1+exp(-k*P + km))` = `P*exp(kP)/(exp(kP) + exp(km))`. This doesn't simplify to standard forms easily.

Let me check candidates with P² and exp(P*c) terms that have no t (or can zero out t):

**Candidate 4**: `P*c0 + P**c1*c2 + c3 + c4*exp(P*c5) + c6*exp(P*c7)`
No t-dependence. Has P^c1 (can be P² or P³), P, constant, and two exponentials. But we need a sigmoid `P/(1+exp(...))`, which can't be built from sum of exponentials and polynomials.

The key challenge: the GT has a term `P/(1+exp(...))` which is a rational function of an exponential. None of the candidates have division by `(1+exp(...))`. The candidates have terms like `exp(P*c)`, `sin(P*c+c)`, `log(P*c+1)`, `P/(P*c+c)`, `1/(P+c)²`, etc.

The sigmoid `1/(1+exp(x))` cannot be expressed as a finite sum of exponentials, polynomials, sines, logs, or simple rational functions. This is a fundamentally different functional form.

GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P/(c9 + exp(-c10*(-c11 + P)))
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and determine which candidates can match it.

## GT Analysis

The GT is:
```
0.13870625668024555*(-1 + P/8.038138014396704)*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*(1 - P/70.01799944958296)*P + 0.13870625668024555*P/(1 + exp(-8.038138014396704*(-0.5894251550796137 + P)))
```

Let me simplify. Let me denote α = 0.13870625668024555, a = 8.038138014396704, b = 70.01799944958296, d = 0.5894251550796137.

**Term 1:** α*(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P
= α*(P/a - 1)*(1 - P/b)*P

**Term 2:** α*(1 - P/b)*P

**Term 3:** α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(-d + P))) = α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P - d)))

This is a sigmoid term: α*P * σ(a*(P-d))

Combining Terms 1 and 2:
α*(1 - P/b)*P * [(-1 + P/a) + 1] = α*(1 - P/b)*P * (P/a)
= (α/a)*(1 - P/b)*P²
= (α/a)*P² - (α/(a*b))*P³

So GT = (α/a)*P² - (α/(a*b))*P³ + α*P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

Numerically:
- α/a ≈ 0.1387/8.038 ≈ 0.01726
- α/(a*b) ≈ 0.1387/(8.038*70.018) ≈ 0.000246
- Sigmoid coefficient: α ≈ 0.1387
- Sigmoid steepness: a ≈ 8.038

So GT = c*P² + d*P³ + e*P*sigmoid(f*(P-g))

The GT has **no dependence on t**. The functional form involves:
- A polynomial in P (P² and P³ terms)
- A sigmoid-weighted P term: P/(1 + exp(-a*(P-d)))

The sigmoid function 1/(1+exp(-x)) cannot be exactly represented by sin, log, simple exponentials, or polynomials.

Now let me check: can the sigmoid P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) be represented by combinations of exp(P*c)?

Note that P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = P*exp(a*(P-d))/(1+exp(a*(P-d))). This is NOT a simple sum of exponentials.

However, we can write:
P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) = P - P/(1+exp(a*(P-d)))

This still involves a sigmoid, not expressible as a finite sum of exp(c*P) terms.

## Key insight
The sigmoid term P/(1+exp(-a*(P-d))) cannot be exactly represented by:
- Polynomials in P
- sin(P*c + c)
- exp(P*c)
- log(P*c + 1)
- 1/P^n
- Any finite combination of these

None of the candidates contain a term of the form P/(1+exp(...)) or any sigmoid-like structure. All candidates use combinations of polynomials, exp, sin, log, and rational functions of P and t.

Since the sigmoid function is linearly independent from all these basis functions, **no candidate can exactly match the GT**.

Let me verify there's no candidate with a denominator involving exp that could create a sigmoid... Looking through all candidates: None have the form anything/(1+exp(...)) or anything/(c+exp(...)). 

Candidate 1 has terms divided by (P*c1 + c2), not involving exp in denominator.

No candidate contains a sigmoid-type term.
